<div id="review_1574055727" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1574055727" />
    <a title="Alyssa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa"><img alt="Alyssa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500935920p2/8472395.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1574055727?book_show_action=true">Mar 08, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Alyssa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alyssa" href="/user/show/8472395-alyssa">Alyssa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8472395-alyssa?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1574055727" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14461428677961292025">REALLY GOOD. And I actually really love that the next two books will be companion sequels, told in the perspective of two different girls. Adelaide's story is very complete and wrapped up. Mira's story, and Tamsin's story... I can't wait to see who is next! Both of them are wonderful characters. <3<br/><br/>Anyway, THIS Mead book really worked for me!<br/><br/><br/><br/>***<a href='http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/03/review-glittering-court-by-richelle-mead.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br/><br/>The Glittering Court by Richelle Mead<br/>Book One of The Glittering Court series<br/>Publisher: Razorbill<br/>Publication Da</span>
  <span id="freeText14461428677961292025" style="display:none">REALLY GOOD. And I actually really love that the next two books will be companion sequels, told in the perspective of two different girls. Adelaide's story is very complete and wrapped up. Mira's story, and Tamsin's story... I can't wait to see who is next! Both of them are wonderful characters. &lt;3<br /><br />Anyway, THIS Mead book really worked for me!<br /><br /><br /><br />***<a href="http://eaterofbooks.blogspot.com/2016/03/review-glittering-court-by-richelle-mead.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Review posted on The Eater of Books! blog</a>***<br /><br />The Glittering Court by Richelle Mead<br />Book One of The Glittering Court series<br />Publisher: Razorbill<br />Publication Date: April 5, 2016<br />Rating: 4 stars<br />Source: Copy provided by First to Read<br /><br />Summary (from Goodreads):<br /><br />A dazzling new fantasy series set in a mix of Elizabethan and frontier worlds that’s dripping with romance from Richelle Mead, #1 internationally bestselling author of Vampire Academy.<br /><br />Big and sweeping, spanning the refined palaces of Osfrid to the gold dust and untamed forests of Adoria, The Glittering Court tells the story of Adelaide, an Osfridian countess who poses as her servant to escape an arranged marriage and start a new life in Adoria, the New World. But to do that, she must join the Glittering Court. <br /><br />Both a school and a business venture, the Glittering Court is designed to transform impoverished girls into upper-class ladies capable of arranging powerful and wealthy marriages in the New World. Adelaide naturally excels in her training and even makes a few friends: the fiery former laundress Tamsin and the beautiful Sirminican refugee Mira. She manages to keep her true identity hidden from all but one: the intriguing Cedric Thorn, son of the wealthy proprietor of the Glittering Court.<br /><br />When Adelaide discovers that Cedric is hiding a dangerous secret of his own, together, they hatch a scheme to make the best of Adelaide’s deception. Complications soon arise—first, as they cross the treacherous seas from Osfrid to Adoria, and later, when Adelaide catches the attention of a powerful governor.<br /><br />But no complication will prove quite as daunting as the potent attraction simmering between Adelaide and Cedric. An attraction that, if acted on, would scandalize the Glittering Court and make them both outcasts in wild, vastly uncharted lands. . . .<br /><br />What I Liked:<br /><br />This book was different! I don't think I've read anything quite like it before. We have a mixture of Elizabethan London (though the setting is a fantasy made-up one) and the American Frontier (1800s, gold panning, the New World, Manifest Destiny, etc.). Everything is purely fantasy, but totally based on these two types of settings, mixed into one. How cool! I really enjoyed the book. This is only my second Mead book (and I wasn't a fan of Soundless), and I'm happy to say that I actually enjoyed this one a lot!<br /><br />Lady Whitmore, a countess, is about to enter an arranged marriage... with her cousin. Her family has no money, but she has a title, and so the match is a balanced one. But Adelaide sets the chance to escape by pretending to be her servant, when her servant is invited to join the Glittering Court (the servant doesn't want to go, but Adelaide does). There, Adelaide is taught how to be nobility (which she obviously excels at), and all the girls are to attract a husband and marry well. She makes friends, including her two roommates, and Cedric Thorn, son of Jasper Thorn, who runs the Glittering Court. Cedric finds out her secret... and she finds out some of his. Together, they begin to figure out how to help Cedric with his secret - but it could mean giving up hers.<br /><br />There are so many parts to this book! I definitely cannot say that this book was boring. The book starts with Adelaide meeting her future husband, and then she hears about the Glittering Court and runs away. Then a lot of time is spent at the Glittering Court. And the girls are taken to the New World to find husbands (that's the whole point of the Glittering Court - to find rich husbands overseas, in the New World). There, everything gets hairy.<br /><br />I like Adelaide! She's tough and bold and has guys. To leave a privileged life of class and riches and entitlement? It seemed like an easy choice given the circumstances, but the learning curve was steep. Nevertheless, Adelaide learns a lot, in terms of how to be a working woman, less than a noblewoman. Which is funny, because the Glittering Court is all about turning working women into noblewomen. <br /><br />I also adore Adelaide's roommates, Tamsin and Mira! Tamsin is determined to be the #1 girl at the Glittering Court (aptly called the diamond). She is trying to do the best because she can't go back to her former life (we don't know her backstory, but it's coming in future books). She is doing everything she can to turn up the charm and secure a man. And whatever her reasons are, we can't blame her! Tamsin knows what's best for her. As ambitious as she is, she's also a good friend. She and Adelaide do not have the easiest friendship at first, but Tamsin redeems herself.<br /><br />I like Mira more than I liked Tamsin, though I liked Tamsin and am really curious about her backstory. I'm really curious about Mira's too though. The way Mead writes this book, we don't know everything about Tamsin and Mira. They'll be the protagonists of each of the next books, so we'll find out things as the series goes on. Mira is of a different ethnic group, and men don't want to marry her or take her seriously. But Mira is so sweet and such a survivor. I like her a lot!<br /><br />Oh Cedric. We meet him fairly quickly, when he comes to Adelaide's house to inform her servant that she has been accepted into the Glittering Court (and that is when Adelaide devises her plan to escape). Cedric is so sweet and protective, and keeps Adelaide's secrets without even knowing her. I love how devoted he becomes to her, and how far he'd go for her. I also really like that he is true to himself and does not fall to peer pressure (you'll have to see what I mean by that).<br /><br />The romance is so slow-burn and wonderful! This book is long, and the author takes her time in crafting the relationship. Adelaide is at the Glittering Court's manor of nearly a year, and then in the New World for about a year too (or thereabout). So basically, she and Cedric get to know each other really well, during the time. During the first year, they're friends, but you can tell that she is attracted to him. But more importantly, she risks a lot to help him, and makes some tough choices, for him. What I will say - no one has to become a martyr for anyone. Cedric does not sacrifice himself for her, and vice versa, at any permanent point in the story (again, you'll have to read the book to see what I mean - and I promise this isn't a spoiler). I really enjoyed the last third of the book, especially in terms of the romance. Things got pretty heated! Also, no love triangle.<br /><br />Did I already mention how much I like the setting? A mixture of an Elizabethan setting, and the Frontier. The gold mining and panning took me by surprise, in the second half of the book! It felt like the Wild West or something. I like this though, the blend of two very different times/worlds/settings! The author did a really good job with crafting the world.<br /><br />Overall, I'm quite pleased with this book. The strong female relationships, the lovely slow-burn romance, the interesting plot, fascinating setting... and the best part? (Or one of them.) This book reads like a standalone. Literally the entire story is told in this book, so you can read this book and stop there! Adelaide and Cedric's story is done, at the end. I mean, they may make cameos in the two companion novels, but their story is pretty final. And I LOVE the ending!<br /><br />What I Did Not Like:<br /><br />This is more of a warning than a dislike -- not everything will make 100% sense. And that is because the sequels will make those things clearer - that's what I'm gathering. Book two and book three are in Tamsin and Mira's POV (though which character is getting which book, I do not know). <br /><br />Would I Recommend It:<br /><br />I liked this book a lot! It's completely historical-esque, but in a fantasy setting (because everything is made up), but there is no paranormal aspect to the book (yay). I like the steamy romance a lot (and no love triangle, woohoo), and the story in general was really cool. Plus, you can read it as a standalone! That's a major win right there.<br /><br />Rating:<br /><br />4 stars. While I am very content with what I read here, I will definitely be looking forward to read Tamsin's story, and Mira's story! Usually I'm kind of wary of companion sequels in YA, but I love how Mead has the series set up. Cedric and Adelaide's ending was perfect!</span>
  <a data-text-id="14461428677961292025" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1441201059" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1441201059" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1441201059?book_show_action=true">Nov 12, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=signed">signed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1441201059" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13071850661508915796"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464733591i/19270113._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>I've read almost everything Richelle Mead has ever written, but I think it's time for me to stop. Do you ever feel like maybe you outgrew an author? I remember buying physical <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859654520' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vampire Academy</a> books at midnight, because they were so magical I couldn't wait! One time, during a move, my new house didn't have internet yet, so I camped out in a McDonald's parking lot at midnight so I could download <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348868431' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Indigo Spell</a>. To this date, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83712988' rel='nofollow noopener'> the Dark Swan series</a> is one the best series I've ever read and is <i>sti</i></span>
  <span id="freeText13071850661508915796" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464733591i/19270113._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I've read almost everything Richelle Mead has ever written, but I think it's time for me to stop. Do you ever feel like maybe you outgrew an author? I remember buying physical <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/859654520" rel="nofollow noopener">Vampire Academy</a> books at midnight, because they were so magical I couldn't wait! One time, during a move, my new house didn't have internet yet, so I camped out in a McDonald's parking lot at midnight so I could download <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/348868431" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Indigo Spell</a>. To this date, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/83712988" rel="nofollow noopener"> the Dark Swan series</a> is one the best series I've ever read and is <i>still</i> the only book starring a shaman I've ever read. <br><br>But then <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/666835985" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloodlines</a> became horrible, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/526876344" rel="nofollow noopener">Gameboard of the Gods</a> was a joke, and I gave <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1354119419" rel="nofollow noopener">Soundless</a> a two star rating when it deserved a one star rating, but I didn't want to believe Richelle Mead, one of my favorite authors of all time, was writing nothing but one star books.<br><br>I have outgrown Richelle Mead, and I don't think I will be reading any more YA stories from her, because my heart can't take giving her more chances and me having to write more negative reviews.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1469234846ra/19795373.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>First off, this book is not a fantasy and should not be marked as one. It's historical fiction with made up names. <br><br>This book is about a countess that has lost her parents. Her new guardian, her grandmother, wants her to marry a cousin so they can keep living their extravagant lifestyle while also keeping the blood pure. Well, this doesn't sit well with our main protagonist, and when a man comes to take one of her servants away to the Glittering Court, she finds a way to take the servant's place.<br><br>Which sounds reasonable, right? Until you realize the man stated what the Glittering Court is - a court that prepares beautiful young woman to become nobleman's wives to the highest bidder. Yeah, bidder. She legitimately escapes her grandmother's arranged marriage to be part of a stranger's arranged marriage. You do find out later in the story that there is more choice and leeway involved, but our dear Adelaide, Osfridian Countess, does not know that upfront. This is the main plot of this book, and it doesn't even make sense. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455986610ra/18176939.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then, let's queue the obvious love interest and add in some angst with it being an unobtainable love. That is, until it's just obtainable and they could have saved everyone a lot of trouble and, more importantly, me a lot of time. <br><br>I will give Richelle Mead a <i>little</i> credit, because she does try to tell a story that would start a discussion on religious freedom. I'll give any author credit if they write something thought provoking that is somewhat taboo to talk about, and she did. That's not saying she wrote about it amazingly, or that this book would change anyone's life, but I still appreciate the sentiment and discussion, because this is a <i>very</i> important topic that our world needs to talk a hell of a lot more about! <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Do you think my being someone else's wife will change anything? Don't you know that I'd lie with you in the groves, under the light of the moon? That I'd defy the laws of gods and men for you?”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I also think it's important to note, that as crazy as the hypocrisy in the first part of this book is, the first part of this book is way more enjoyable than the later parts. The ending of this book has probably the biggest use of deus ex machina I have read in a really long time. I hate "big shiny bow" syndrome in my stories, and this book is the queen of them. This story is one hopeless situation after hopeless situation that always ends up being fixed in a blink of an eye and with a snap of someone's fingers. <br><br>I believe this book is going to have two companion novels. I'm sure the two companion novels are going to be in the POV of the two girls Adelaide befriends in the Glittering Court. These girls have a lot of mystery going on behind the scenes, while Adelaide was off trying to get married, so the idea is kind of appealing to me. This book also ended with a clean ending, while still leaving a few mini cliffhanger mysteries to make the reader want to read whatever comes next. <br><br>I never want to discourage anyone from reading something. This didn't work for me, but hopefully it could still work for you. I have never read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10507293.The_Selection__The_Selection___1_" rel="nofollow noopener">The Selection</a>, but all my friends say that if you like that series, you will also like this one. <br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13071850661508915796" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina  Kondrenko" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina  Kondrenko" href="/user/show/36306002-katerina-kondrenko">Katerina  Kondrenko</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1427006339" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7590355162264805233"><b>
  <blockquote>2 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br/><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br/><a href='http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/04/the-glittering-court-by-richelle-mead.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br/><br/><b>Genre</b>: high-fantasy, YA<br/><b>Stuff</b>: historical hints, bride-market<br/><b>Fail</b>: boring story and characters<br/><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br/><b>Love-Geometry</b>: seeming<br/><br/><b>Quote-Core</b>: <i><blockquote>“We’re all in charge of our own lives—and we have to live with the consequences of the choices we make.”</blockquote> </i><br/>Buddy-DNF with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/comment/show/151015646' rel='nofollow noopener'>Nastassja</a>.<br/><br/>I rarel</span>
  <span id="freeText7590355162264805233" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>2 out of 10</blockquote>
</b><br><b>Ревью в моем блоге/This review on my blog<br><a href="http://living-a-thousand-lives.blogspot.ru/2016/04/the-glittering-court-by-richelle-mead.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Living A Thousand Lives</a></b> <i>(please use Chrome/Yandex browser or Android/IOS to see the page; otherwise, spoiler-tags I use to make my post compact may not work)</i><br><br><b>Genre</b>: high-fantasy, YA<br><b>Stuff</b>: historical hints, bride-market<br><b>Fail</b>: boring story and characters<br><b>POV</b>: 1st-person, female<br><b>Love-Geometry</b>: seeming<br><br><b>Quote-Core</b>: <i><blockquote>“We’re all in charge of our own lives—and we have to live with the consequences of the choices we make.”</blockquote> </i><br>Buddy-DNF with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/comment/show/151015646" rel="nofollow noopener">Nastassja</a>.<br><br>I rarely DNF books (12 titles only during my whole life), I can skip boring passages (it happens rarely as well) or even pages (almost never) to help myself through, but in this particular case...<br><br><div>
  <br>
  <a href="https://1.bp.blogspot.com/-syV7LDVgn_M/VyrtCHTFnlI/AAAAAAAAApk/dc-kn_xX60EBF_GcluZjw78TU_umEY6jwCLcB/s1600/tumblr_inline_nz84aqqQka1qfjd3v_500.gif" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img height="172" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1462969753ra/19066318.gif" width="320" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</div><br><br>I just can't take it anymore.<br><br>This story has a great premise, it promises a pseudo-historical setting, steamy romance, and a strong heroine, but everything is a lie. I mean, the high-fantasy world turns out being a lot like the real one, the romance is boring, the main characters are flat, and I can't find anything to hold on to and finish the book.<br><br>We have a <b>noble but poor lady</b>, who has to become a wife of a not very pleasant boy her grandma nicely chose. Trying to escape the arrange marriage, she goes to the <i>Glittering Court</i> (using her servant's name), a school for common girls those are eager to sail abroad and be sold to rich men of the New World. They would learn how to dance, walk, talk and so on in da style of a high society lady, after that they would take exams and their code-names aka quality labels (brilliant, for example, is for the best, while amethyst is for a so-so girl). Yes, this the place where our lover of freedom goes, 'cause bride-markets are all about freedom, aren't they? I don't get MC's logic, but she was desperate and maybe it was the reason of this not very clever move.<br><br>Also we have <b>Cedric</b>. A son of the owner of the <i>Glittering Court</i> and <b>Adelaide</b>'s (false name of the MC) recruiter. He has a BIG secret which is quite serious they say, but only say, not show. His religion is different from the main one like Eastern Orthodoxy is different from Catholicism (not a really big deal, I mean). In the book's world someone like Cedric is a heretic and supposed to be burned at the stake (or something like that). I didn't give a damn about his secret and potential consequences of it's revelation, 'cause we've seen no executions, no tortures, nothing at all what could show us how dangerous was to believe in the things Cedric did.<br> <br>Between Adelaide and Cedric is not an instalove, it's an <b>all-of-a-sudden-love</b>. They are falling for each other with passing of time, but we aren't there to see the processes, because this book has holes in a form of "six months later", "after a year" and other time-black-spots during those MC is forging relationships with girls at the school and with Cedric too. And how are we supposed to feel something toward strangers? To say 'a year passed' is not a way to relate your characters to your readers.<br><br>Because of these jumps through time, I was constantly irritated with so-called Adelaide's friends, her goals and reasons (to do anything for a man with a different religion vision, 'cause he was in danger we readers were only told about and never showed with) and with the things those were going on. Or weren't. To be honest, <i>The Glittering Court</i> is a very static story: decorations change, the rest of it doesn't. And there's no intrigue, nothing to make you want, to be eager for more information, to read faster, to discuss something with people.<br><br>That's why I gave up at 53%, rated it with 2/10 stars, and not gonna read next books in this series too.<br><br><b>The Glittering Court (Сверкающий двор):</b><br><blockquote>— <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1427006339" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glittering Court (Сверкающий двор)</a> #1/3<br>— Untitled (Без названия) #2/3<br>— Untitled (Без названия) #3/3</blockquote></span>
  <a data-text-id="7590355162264805233" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1593912744" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1593912744" />
    <a title="Nastassja" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja"><img alt="Nastassja" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1596034018p2/7734134.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1593912744?book_show_action=true">Mar 29, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nastassja" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nastassja" href="/user/show/7734134-nastassja">Nastassja</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">no one</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fell-short-of-expectations">fell-short-of-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=2016">2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7734134-nastassja?shelf=these-two-are-terrible-together">these-two-are-terrible-together</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1593912744" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3075028036236839061"><p>
  <b>Actual rating: 1.5 stars</b>
  <br/>
</p><p>
  <i>
    <b> DNF at about 53%</b>
  </i>
  <br/>
</p><p>Welcome to a <i>fancy brothel</i>! Every kind of girl is available here for a good price. Have a pick. <br/></p><p>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428477048ra/14430548.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</p><p>Our MC is <i>the Countess of Rothford</i>. Her life is pretty hard: she has to marry an itching nasty cousin or stay moneyless heiress and loose her grand fancy house *gasp* what a terrible fate! How will our poor baby find a way out of this situation? Will she decide to stay poor but, at least, save her pride and title? Or will she marry her</p></span>
  <span id="freeText3075028036236839061" style="display:none"><p>
  <b>Actual rating: 1.5 stars</b>
  <br>
</p><p>
  <i>
    <b> DNF at about 53%</b>
  </i>
  <br>
</p><p>Welcome to a <i>fancy brothel</i>! Every kind of girl is available here for a good price. Have a pick. <br></p><p>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1428477048ra/14430548.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</p><p>Our MC is <i>the Countess of Rothford</i>. Her life is pretty hard: she has to marry an itching nasty cousin or stay moneyless heiress and loose her grand fancy house *gasp* what a terrible fate! How will our poor baby find a way out of this situation? Will she decide to stay poor but, at least, save her pride and title? Or will she marry her terrible cousin? No. <i>She will steal her maids identity and enlist into a fancy brothel called The Glittering Court where women are shipped into a foreign country and sold to rich men.</i> Wow, that is the best option ever! Independence and comfort life are on the way. Oh no, stop, I forgot to mention <b>a working house for girls who refuse to play along with fancy brothel's rules</b> (and something tells me she'll choose not to marry another itchy man). Such a freedom, indeed! For the love of god, I can't fathom <u>why abandoning your responsibility and going to an unknown country with no means and utter dependence on other people's mercy is better than staying home and facing your problems?</u> Simply put: exchanging one problem for a whole carriage of problems.<br><i><blockquote>But honestly? Who’d pick those kind of long work hours over a chance to be on the arm of a wealthy, doting husband who’ll drape you in silks and jewels?</blockquote></i><br>Any sane being would choose the first option but <i>Ada</i> (it's her maid's name and we don't even know her real one) is <b>a selfish, fickle creature</b>. <i>Now tell me, author, why should I care about a heroine who cares only about herself, betrays her friends easily when it suits her and has no doubts about her own awesomeness</i> <s>*standing ovations*</s> *throws tomatos*<br></p><p>Nothing happens in the book except for <b>balls</b>, and discussions of all kind of <b>ball gowns</b> and <b>ball related conversations</b>. Ballocks, what a waste of book space! <br></p><p>Oh, wait, I forgot to tell you about <i>Cedric</i> - main love interest, who has this terrible secret that can be his undoing. *whispers* he's <b>a heretic</b> *gasp* No shit!<br><i><blockquote>“I believe the six wayward angels are every bit as holy as the six glorious ones. They aren’t demons. And I believe divinity is all around us in the natural world, free to anyone,” he said calmly. “Not something only accessible through the priests in their churches.”</blockquote></i><br>So, you are saying that he is, simply put, <i>a hippy</i>? And that, um, in his country hippies are <b>illegal and punishable by death</b>? So, these people live in the 18th or 19th century but act like they are from <i>Middle Ages</i>. Bloody hell, people, don't you have more important issues to fight?! <i>Heretics are your major Government level problem?!</i> *facepalm* What a nonsense! Religious stuff is always hard to interpret, so readers would accept it and understand the importance of it in a book, but this absurd is beyond my comprehension. <br></p><p>To summarize my opinion about this book:<br><i><blockquote>“Do you think my future’s a joke? Is all of this a joke to you?”</blockquote></i><br>What do you think is my answer?<br></p><p>*******************************<br><b>Pre-review</b><br>No more. this book feels like torture. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1427006339" rel="nofollow noopener">Katerina</a> and I tried to slay the dragon, but the fucking dragon is unkillable. </p></span>
  <a data-text-id="3075028036236839061" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1426350732?book_show_action=true">Oct 27, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wanderlust_Wanz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wanderlust_Wanz" href="/user/show/24809866-wanderlust-wanz">Wanderlust_Wanz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/24809866-wanderlust-wanz?shelf=young-adult-dystopia-fantasy-scifi">young-adult-dystopia-fantasy-scifi</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1426350732" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15860512226511411349">The Glittering Court is quite an enjoyable read, with its rather intriguing premise and slow-building romance between Adelaide and Cedric. Though there were some flaws present such as slow pacing and certain loopholes, I still enjoyed it as a whole regardless. <br/><br/>Things started to get more interesting when Adelaide departed to Adoria after receiving ample etiquette trainings where she met with other potential and noteworthy suitors, or so she thought as things started to go downhill for her. Still,</span>
  <span id="freeText15860512226511411349" style="display:none">The Glittering Court is quite an enjoyable read, with its rather intriguing premise and slow-building romance between Adelaide and Cedric. Though there were some flaws present such as slow pacing and certain loopholes, I still enjoyed it as a whole regardless. <br /><br />Things started to get more interesting when Adelaide departed to Adoria after receiving ample etiquette trainings where she met with other potential and noteworthy suitors, or so she thought as things started to go downhill for her. Still, I liked how brave she is at the very beginning when she was willing to forgo her status in order to escape her undesirable marriage and daringly disguise her way into Adoria. Also, the friendship that she eventually forged with Tamsin and Mira whom she later befriended in Adoria was heartening too. <br /><br />The ending portion of the story was exceptionally exciting as things took an unexpected and intense turn. Also, I was finally convinced of the romance between Adelaide and Cedric, which I was initially doubtful of, as they managed to overcome their obstacles together and forged a more solid and endearing relationship. </span>
  <a data-text-id="15860512226511411349" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

<span id="freeTextContainer11214962045616264069">4.5 stars<br/><br/>I loved the premise and hello gorgeous cover, so I was eager to start this book.   <span id="freeText11214962045616264069" style="display:none">4.5 stars<br /><br />I loved the premise and hello gorgeous cover, so I was eager to start this book. Once I got started, I tried to take my time because I wanted to savor it. <br /><br />Love love love Adelaide. She's sassy and fantastically outspoken for the time period. Her BFFs Tamsin and Mira were just as delightful and I really enjoyed all of the scenes with the three of them. And Cedric...he's a whole other story. The UST between him and Adelaide is so delicious. There are some of the sweetest swoons and their banter had me grinning. <br /><br />Plot wise, there is a lot going on. Like a lot a lot. And that's where my attention started to wane a bit. The ending isn't cliffhangery at all, but there is definitely a set up for the next book. I can't wait to see what happens next. </span>

<div id="review_1425943906" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1425943906" />
    <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews"><img alt="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1468898958p2/12502667.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1425943906?book_show_action=true">Oct 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel  (APCB Reviews)" href="/user/show/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews">Rachel  (APCB Reviews)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/12502667-rachel-apcb-reviews?shelf=2016-releases">2016-releases</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1425943906" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18177303988037370709">I've been a longtime fan of Richelle Mead, and although this is completely unlike any of her other works, I found myself completely delighted by her latest series starter, The Glittering Court. It has so many fascinating components weaved together in a way that somehow works. With strong characters, adorable romance, and many intertwined plot conflicts, this series definitely has a lot going for it.<br/><br/>Wanting to escape a loveless pending marriage and a stifling lifestyle, Adelaide assumes her serva</span>
  <span id="freeText18177303988037370709" style="display:none">I've been a longtime fan of Richelle Mead, and although this is completely unlike any of her other works, I found myself completely delighted by her latest series starter, The Glittering Court. It has so many fascinating components weaved together in a way that somehow works. With strong characters, adorable romance, and many intertwined plot conflicts, this series definitely has a lot going for it.<br /><br />Wanting to escape a loveless pending marriage and a stifling lifestyle, Adelaide assumes her servant's identity to join the Glittering Court, a business and finishing school that takes low-class girls and transforms them into educated, proper women fit to marry wealthy men looking for wives in the new Osfridian colonies across the treacherous sea. As Adelaide struggles to hide her true identity, she must spin even more lies and sometimes hurt the ones she loves.<br /><br />The main character, Adelaide is a witty, highly opinionated person. I love her tenacity and will to change her fate. It was quite comical seeing her learn how to do such mundane tasks such as mending and cleaning dishes. Cedric, the Glittering Court owner's son, is an intellect and extremely kind gentleman. I felt their connection from the very beginning, and I love their sassy banter and electrifying chemistry.<br /><br />As much as I enjoyed the romance, the friendships in this novel surpass that. I wish more books would contain wonderful friendships like this book does. Tamsin is a fiery, driven, and ambitious person who has a sentimental and fiercely protective side. Mira has so much inner strength and wisdom. Together the three work together and support one another. I love this friendship, and I'm so glad Richelle included it in her story.<br /><br />I felt this book had three distinct parts. At first I was immediately swept up in the world-building and the pretty dresses and opulence. Eventually the pace slowed down for me as they entered the voyage section of the book, but it quickly picked up again. This book went through highs and lows in terms of pacing, but overall it was an easy, engaging read.<br /><br />This book had so many fascinating elements. I really liked how this book had influences of Elizabethan culture yet later on in the book there's a new frontier/wild west vibe. Of course the scenes of luxury especially piqued my fancy. There is a large cast of characters, and I had a bit of trouble keeping up with all of them. I was also expecting a bit more from the fantasy label of this book, but there are no magical or supernatural elements.<br /><br />I'm pretty sure the next two books will follow Tamsin or Mira as Adelaide's storyline is resolved by the end of this book. I'm curious, so I'll definitely continue with this series. If you're into books with historical settings, great friendships, and a great lead main character, I think you'd like this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18177303988037370709" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7728753247376172376"><b>I expanded on this review a lot in my video review: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mNOLnAfvYSg'>https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mNOLn...</a></b><br/><br/>Edit: I just can't. It has to be 3 stars.<br/><br/>This is a 3.5 stars. I have never more than now wanted there to be half ratings on GR because 3 is too low and 4 is too high. But I'm going to round UP for this book because I feel like the book is rated low enough. But this may change. <br/><br/>So I filmed a spoiler-free video review for this book because I really felt the need to discuss my feelings out loud, and also not</span>
  <span id="freeText7728753247376172376" style="display:none"><b>I expanded on this review a lot in my video review: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mNOLnAfvYSg">https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=mNOLn...</a></b><br /><br />Edit: I just can't. It has to be 3 stars.<br /><br />This is a 3.5 stars. I have never more than now wanted there to be half ratings on GR because 3 is too low and 4 is too high. But I'm going to round UP for this book because I feel like the book is rated low enough. But this may change. <br /><br />So I filmed a spoiler-free video review for this book because I really felt the need to discuss my feelings out loud, and also not to type them up.<br /><br />But the short version is: this book was GOOD but there was too much useless plot. This book follows a girl who wants to escape her royal life and ends up going to the Glittering Court which teaches "common" girls how to be royalty, and then they are sold on a different continent to men needing wives. That is a good plot, and that aspect of the story was good. But Mead added all these sub plots that were really in the background and not well explained or expanded or developed so the book just had too much of nothing in it. A lot of plots she added that she didn't know what to do with and ended abruptly. There are even mini cliff hanger endings to make a second book necessary when it's really really not necessary. This didn't need to be more than a stand alone. <br /><br />So while I enjoyed this and thought it was good, I didn't really "like" it because i'm not really sure what of what I read was important.</span>

<div id="review_1444267617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1444267617" />
    <a title="Jennifer" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer"><img alt="Jennifer" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1394406877p2/2473504.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1444267617?book_show_action=true">Nov 16, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jennifer" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jennifer" href="/user/show/2473504-jennifer">Jennifer</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=i-met-the-author">i-met-the-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=dropped-series">dropped-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=overrated-imo">overrated-imo</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=young-adult-genre">young-adult-genre</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=read-2016">read-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2473504-jennifer?shelf=listened-to-audiobook">listened-to-audiobook</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1444267617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10256734927110039573">★★½<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272506.The_Glittering_Court__The_Glittering_Court___1_' title='The Glittering Court (The Glittering Court, #1) by Richelle Mead' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Glittering Court</a> is the first installment in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/137902.Richelle_Mead' title='Richelle Mead' rel='nofollow noopener'>Richelle Mead</a>'s series titled (surprise, surprise) <u>The Glittering Court</u>. At this point in my reviews, I would have listed the genres but I kinda have a problem. It is marketed as a fantasy but I find this severely misleading. <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272506.The_Glittering_Court__The_Glittering_Court___1_' title='The Glittering Court (The Glittering Court, #1) by Richelle Mead' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Glittering Court</a> is historical fiction with conveniently made-up names for the countries and oceans. There is no fantasy in this book. As for historical fiction, it wasn't bad. I liked the first half very much actually</span>
  <span id="freeText10256734927110039573" style="display:none">★★½<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272506.The_Glittering_Court__The_Glittering_Court___1_" title="The Glittering Court (The Glittering Court, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glittering Court</a> is the first installment in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/137902.Richelle_Mead" title="Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Richelle Mead</a>'s series titled (surprise, surprise) <u>The Glittering Court</u>. At this point in my reviews, I would have listed the genres but I kinda have a problem. It is marketed as a fantasy but I find this severely misleading. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272506.The_Glittering_Court__The_Glittering_Court___1_" title="The Glittering Court (The Glittering Court, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glittering Court</a> is historical fiction with conveniently made-up names for the countries and oceans. There is no fantasy in this book. As for historical fiction, it wasn't bad. I liked the first half very much actually. I could easily relate to the main character, even with her "It ain't easy being rich and royal" attitude. I wanted her to be happy and even though the consequences to her chosen problem solving were painfully predictable, it was fun to read. Maybe Ms. Mead realized how predictable it was becoming too so she mixed things up later on. I don't know what happened but <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272506.The_Glittering_Court__The_Glittering_Court___1_" title="The Glittering Court (The Glittering Court, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glittering Court</a> became less fun and more of a chore to read for me personally. My initial four-star review plummeted to two and a half. I added the half star because I genuinely enjoyed this book when I started it. I wish my enjoyment had lasted but that's the way it goes sometimes. <br /><br />If you are a fan of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/137902.Richelle_Mead" title="Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">Richelle Mead</a> in general, then try <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27272506.The_Glittering_Court__The_Glittering_Court___1_" title="The Glittering Court (The Glittering Court, #1) by Richelle Mead" rel="nofollow noopener">The Glittering Court</a>. Continuing this series is definitely not in the cards for me but maybe you'll have better luck :)<br /><br /><b>My favorite quote:</b><br /><i>"Bad things are always going to happen. There's no way to avoid that. Our control comes in how we face them."<i></i></i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10256734927110039573" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('paBOtF92GKcfUtcsvY198aJ9FnZjn6thsohz3l/iqeWv2yl1RQHusg/59driiyZJ9uGDw/qvWsMG5f9SOXBOng==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BwtgQSkZS2GDanP1CnkNaiDPbtI6zxMiapj2SkRSD1gNcAeAM269dJPBUQNVf1bSdFP7Z6P/4oDe9XrGIsDoIw==')})
  }
//]]>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer13727410951845812041">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br/><br/>A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away f</span>
  <span id="freeText13727410951845812041" style="display:none">Scorpio Richelle Mead is a New York Times and USA Today bestselling author of urban fantasy books for both adults and teens. Originally from Michigan, Richelle now lives in Seattle, Washington where she works on her three series full-time: Georgina Kincaid, Dark Swan, and Vampire Academy.<br /><br />A life-long reader, Richelle has always loved mythology and folklore. When she can actually tear herself away from books (either reading or writing them), she enjoys bad reality TV, traveling, trying interesting cocktails, and shopping for dresses. She's a self-professed coffee addict and has a passion for all things wacky and humorous.<br /></span>
